# Built and iterated on a geocoding divergence Quarto report with interactive leaflet maps, search, divergence lines, and recommendation review layers (showing both preferred and rejected points per facility). Added `geocode_source_preference()` (now populated with 45 hand-reviewed entries from geocode-source-preferences.txt.r: 25 Google, 16 Vera, 3 Marshall, 1 manual) and `geocode_manual_coordinates()` override mechanisms to `build_geocoded_all()`, reducing divergent facilities from 147 to 102. Created CSV archive targets for Google and unified geocoded data. Added address cleaning to `geocode_roster()` for territories and redundant suffixes. Applied multiple address patches in `address_patches()` in `clean.R` (San Diego Staging, JTF Camp Six, Burleigh County, Lincoln County Jail, Otero County Detention, Winn Correctional Center) and hold room address patches in `hold_stub_address_patches()` (Etowah/Gadsden, Knoxville, St. George, Imperial Sub Office corrected, Las Vegas Hold Room). Renamed facility 39 via `canonical_name_overrides_table()` and 1193 via `.ddp_facility_patches()`. Conducted a systematic line-by-line review of all 66 divergent facilities >4 km. Corrected an incorrect manual match in `ddp_manual_strong_matches()` that linked EPSSFTX ("El Paso Soft-Sided Facility") to canonical 108 ("Camp East Montana") — these are distinct facilities. Saved a backup of the canonical ID registry for verification after pipeline rebuild.

All three are coded **IGSA** in FY26, but historically:

- **Joe Corley (182)** and **Louisiana ICE Processing (221)**: IGSA in every year on record.
- **CLIPC (208)**: DIGSA from FY10–FY25, switching to **IGSA only in FY26**. This looks like a reclassification — CLIPC was a dedicated facility (operated by GEO Group) that ICE apparently recategorized as an intergovernmental service agreement.

So the range is **IGSA and DIGSA**, with the DIGSA→IGSA change at CLIPC being the only variation.

<div><tool-call id="toolu_01K1YTZrfc886x2u7ow1BkhW"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"name":"runCode","input":{"code":"facilities_geocoded_all |> \n  filter(divergent) |> \n  head(5)\n","intent":"Check what divergent rows look like"},"intent":"Check what divergent rows look like","inputPreview":{"type":"code","value":"facilities_geocoded_all |> \n  filter(divergent) |> \n  head(5)\n","language":"r"}}</script></tool-call></div>

<div><tool-result call-id="toolu_01DJmgR8tfiPFWqdKifUL7eP"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"status":"success","result":{"type":"text","value":"[File: 7.8KB, 201 lines, showing lines 1-201]\n     1→# Geocode facilities using Google Map...[truncated, total 9127 chars]"},"resultPreview":{"type":"code","value":"[File: 7.8KB, 201 lines, showing lines 1-201]\n# Geocode facilities using Google Maps via ggmap, then merge with\n# source-provided coordinates (Marshall Project, Vera Institute) and\n# flag divergences.\n#\n# Two pipeline functions:\n#   geocode_roster()      — sends all roster addresses to Google Maps API\n#   build_geocoded_all()  — merges Google + source coords, flags issues\n#\n# Requires: register_google(key = Sys.getenv(\"google_maps_api_key\")) called\n# before tar_make(), or set in _targets.R.\n\n# ── Haversine distance (km) ──────────────────────────────────────────────────\n# Vectorized great-circle distance between two (lat, lon) pairs.\n\n.haversine_km <- function(lat1, lon1, lat2, lon2) {\n  R <- 6371\n  to_rad <- pi / 180\n  dlat <- (lat2 - lat1) * to_rad\n  dlon <- (lon2 - lon1) * to_rad\n  a <- sin(dlat / 2)^2 +\n    cos(lat1 * to_rad) * cos(lat2 * to_rad) * sin(dlon / 2)^2\n  R * 2 * atan2(sqrt(a), sqrt(1 - a))\n}\n\n# ── Google Maps geocoding for entire roster ──────────────────────────────────\n# Geocodes every facility in facility_roster that has at least a city.\n# Returns a table with canonical_id, address_string, google_lat, google_lon.\n#\n# Wire this target with cue = tar_cue(mode = \"never\") to avoid re-geocoding.\n# To re-run: targets::tar_invalidate(facilities_google_geocoded); tar_make()\n\ngeocode_roster <- function(facility_roster) {\n  ggmap::register_google(key = Sys.getenv(\"google_maps_api_key\"), write = FALSE)\n\n  to_geocode <- facility_roster |>\n    dplyr::filter(!is.na(facility_city)) |>\n    dplyr::mutate(\n      address_string = dplyr::if_else(\n        !is.na(facility_address),\n        paste(facility_address, facility_city, facility_state, facility_zip,\n              \"USA\", sep = \", \"),\n        paste(facility_city, facility_state, \"USA\", sep = \", \")\n      )\n    ) |>\n    dplyr::select(canonical_id, address_string)\n\n  geocoded <- ggmap::mutate_geocode(to_geocode, address_string)\n\n  geocoded |>\n    dplyr::transmute(\n      canonical_id,\n      address_string,\n      google_lat = lat,\n      google_lon = lon\n    )\n}\n\n\n# ── Unified geocoded table with divergence flags ─────────────────────────────\n# Merges Google geocoding results with source-provided coordinates from\n# Marshall Project and Vera Institute. Flags address quality issues and\n# divergences between sources.\n#\n# For facilities where Google and a source agree within 1 km, lat/lon are set\n# from Google. For facilities with only one source, that source is used.\n# For divergent rows (>1 km apart), lat/lon are NA pending manual review.\n#\n# Returns one row per canonical_id with columns:\n#   canonical_id, google_lat, google_lon, source_lat, source_lon, source_name,\n#   lat, lon, geocode_source, divergence_km, address_quality\n\nbuild_geocoded_all <- function(facility_roster,\n                               facilities_google_geocoded,\n                               hold_canonical_data,\n                               vera_facilities,\n                               detloc_lookup) {\n\n  DIVERGENCE_THRESHOLD_KM <- 1\n\n  # ── Classify address quality ──\n  quality <- facility_roster |>\n    dplyr::transmute(\n      canonical_id,\n      address_quality = dplyr::case_when(\n        is.na(facility_address) & is.na(facility_city) ~ \"no_address\",\n        is.na(facility_address) ~ \"city_only\",\n        grepl(\"^P\\\\.?\\\\s*O\\\\.?\\\\s*Box\", facility_address, ignore.case = TRUE) ~\n          \"po_box\",\n        TRUE ~ \"full\"\n      )\n    )\n\n  # ── Collect source-provided coordinates ──\n  # Marshall Project: hold facilities\n  marshall <- hold_canonical_data$hold_canonical |>\n    dplyr::filter(!is.na(lat)) |>\n    dplyr::transmute(canonical_id, source_lat = lat, source_lon = lon,\n                     source_name = \"marshall_project\")\n\n  # Vera Institute: via detloc\n  vera_coords <- vera_facilities |>\n    dplyr::filter(!is.na(latitude), !is.na(longitude)) |>\n    dplyr::select(detloc, vera_lat = latitude, vera_lon = longitude) |>\n    dplyr::distinct(detloc, .keep_all = TRUE)\n\n  vera_via_detloc <- facility_roster |>\n    dplyr::filter(!is.na(detloc)) |>\n    dplyr::select(canonical_id, detloc) |>\n    dplyr::inner_join(vera_coords, by = \"detloc\") |>\n    dplyr::transmute(canonical_id, source_lat = vera_lat, source_lon = vera_lon,\n                     source_name = \"vera_institute\")\n\n  # Combine sources; prefer Marshall over Vera when both exist for same ID\n  source_coords <- dplyr::bind_rows(marshall, vera_via_detloc) |>\n    dplyr::arrange(canonical_id,\n                   match(source_name, c(\"marshall_project\", \"vera_institute\"))) |>\n    dplyr::distinct(canonical_id, .keep_all = TRUE)\n\n  # ── Merge everything ──\n  result <- facility_roster |>\n    dplyr::select(canonical_id, canonical_name) |>\n    dplyr::left_join(quality, by = \"canonical_id\") |>\n    dplyr::left_join(\n      facilities_google_geocoded |>\n        dplyr::select(canonical_id, google_lat, google_lon),\n      by = \"canonical_id\"\n    ) |>\n    dplyr::left_join(source_coords, by = \"canonical_id\")\n\n  # ── Compute divergence ──\n  has_both <- !is.na(result$google_lat) & !is.na(result$source_lat)\n\n  result$divergence_km <- NA_real_\n  result$divergence_km[has_both] <- .haversine_km(\n    result$google_lat[has_both], result$google_lon[has_both],\n    result$source_lat[has_both], result$source_lon[has_both]\n  )\n\n  # ── Assign lat/lon ──\n  # When both sources exist and agree (<= threshold): use Google\n\n  # When only Google exists: use Google\n  # When only source exists: use source\n  # When divergent (> threshold): leave NA for manual review\n  result <- result |>\n    dplyr::mutate(\n      divergent = !is.na(divergence_km) & divergence_km > DIVERGENCE_THRESHOLD_KM,\n      lat = dplyr::case_when(\n        divergent ~ NA_real_,\n        !is.na(google_lat) ~ google_lat,\n        !is.na(source_lat) ~ source_lat,\n        TRUE ~ NA_real_\n      ),\n      lon = dplyr::case_when(\n        divergent ~ NA_real_,\n        !is.na(google_lon) ~ google_lon,\n        !is.na(source_lon) ~ source_lon,\n        TRUE ~ NA_real_\n      ),\n      geocode_source = dplyr::case_when(\n        divergent ~ \"divergent\",\n        !is.na(google_lat) & !is.na(source_lat) ~ paste0(\"google_maps+\", source_name),\n        !is.na(google_lat) ~ \"google_maps\",\n        !is.na(source_lat) ~ source_name,\n        TRUE ~ NA_character_\n      )\n    )\n\n  # ── Console reporting ──\n  n_total      <- nrow(result)\n  n_no_address <- sum(result$address_quality == \"no_address\", na.rm = TRUE)\n  n_city_only  <- sum(result$address_quality == \"city_only\", na.rm = TRUE)\n  n_po_box     <- sum(result$address_quality == \"po_box\", na.rm = TRUE)\n  n_no_coords  <- sum(is.na(result$lat) & !result$divergent, na.rm = TRUE)\n  n_divergent  <- sum(result$divergent, na.rm = TRUE)\n  n_geocoded   <- sum(!is.na(result$lat))\n\n  cli::cli_inform(c(\n    \"i\" = \"Geocoded {n_geocoded} of {n_total} facilities\",\n    \"!\" = \"{n_no_address} with no address or city (cannot geocode)\",\n    \"!\" = \"{n_city_only} with city only (no street address)\",\n    \"!\" = \"{n_po_box} with P.O. Box addresses\",\n    \"!\" = \"{n_divergent} with Google vs. source divergence > {DIVERGENCE_THRESHOLD_KM} km (lat/lon set to NA)\"\n  ))\n\n  if (n_divergent > 0) {\n    div_rows <- result |>\n      dplyr::filter(divergent) |>\n      dplyr::arrange(dplyr::desc(divergence_km))\n    cli::cli_inform(\"Divergent facilities:\")\n    for (i in seq_len(nrow(div_rows))) {\n      cli::cli_inform(c(\"*\" = \"{div_rows$canonical_name[i]} (ID {div_rows$canonical_id[i]}): {round(div_rows$divergence_km[i], 1)} km — source: {div_rows$source_name[i]}\"))\n    }\n  }\n\n  result |>\n    dplyr::select(canonical_id, canonical_name, lat, lon, geocode_source,\n                  google_lat, google_lon, source_lat, source_lon, source_name,\n                  divergence_km, address_quality, divergent)\n}\n"},"elapsedMs":41}</script></tool-result></div>

4326\n)\n```\n\n```{r}\n#| label: divergence-map\n#| fig-height: 8\nmapview(\n  lines_sf,\n  color = \"gray40\",\n  lwd = 2,\n  layer.name = \"Divergence\",\n  popup = leafpop::popupTable(\n All dependencies are available. Here's what I created:

**`geocoding-divergence.qmd`** with three sections:

1. **Summary** — three tables: geocode source breakdown, address quality breakdown, and divergent facility counts by source (Vera vs. Marshall)
2. **Divergence map** — interactive mapview showing line segments from Google (blue) to source (red) coordinates, with popup details on click
3. **Divergent facilities** — full table sorted by divergence distance, with addresses and both coordinate pairs

The `tar_quarto` target `geocoding_divergence_report` was added to `_targets.R` just after the existing `facility_summary_report`. It will re-render automatically when `facilities_geocoded_all` or `facility_roster` change upstream.

You can render it standalone with `quarto render geocoding-divergence.qmd`, or through the pipeline with `tar_make(geocoding_divergence_report)`.




## User

Okay, let's include address infromation in facilities_geocoded_all and show it in the popups in geocoding-divergence.qmd

Two changes:

1. **`R/geocode.R`** — `build_geocoded_all()` now carries `facility_address`, `facility_city`, `facility_state`, and `facility_zip` through from `facility_roster` into the output. These are selected at the initial join and included in the final `select()`.

2. **`geocoding-divergence.qmd`** — No longer needs to join `facility_roster` separately. All three popup layers (lines, Google points, source points) now show address fields. The bottom table also includes ZIP.

You'll need to rebuild the `facilities_geocoded_all` target to pick up the new columns: `tar_make(facilities_geocoded_all)`. After that, the report can be rendered.

label: build-divergent-data\ndivergent <- facilities_geocoded_all |>\n  filter(divergent)\n```\n\n```{r}\n#| label: build-map-features\n# Build line segments connecting Google → source for each divergent facility\nlines_list <- lapply(seq_len(nrow(divergent)), function(i) {\n  row <- divergent[i, ]\n  st_linestring(matrix(\n    c(row$google_lon, row$source_lon,\n      row$google_lat, source_name, divergence_km = round(divergence_km, 1))\n\nlines_sf <- st_sf(\n  popup_df,\n  geometry = st_sfc(lines_list, crs = 4326)\n)\n\n# Google points (blue)\ngoogle_sf <- st_as_sf(\n  divergent |> filter(!is.na(google_lat)),\n  coords = c(\"google_lon\", \"google_lat\"), crs = 4326\n)\n\n# Source points (red)\nsource_sf <- st_as_sf(\n  divergent |> filter(!is.na(source_lat)),\n  coords = c(\"source_lon\", \"source_lat\"), crs = 4326\n)\n```\n\n```{r}\n#| label: divergence-map\n#| fig-height: 8\npoint_popup_cols <- c(\"canonical_id\", \"canonical_name\",\n                      \"facility_address\", \"facility_city\", \"facility_state\",\n                      \"source_name\", \"divergence_km\")\n\nmapview(\n  lines_sf,\n  color = \"gray40\",\n  lwd = 2,\n  layer.name = \"Divergence\",\n  popup = leafpop::popupTable(\n    lines_sf |> st_drop_geometry(),\n    feature.id = FALSE, row.numbers = FALSE\n  )\n) +\n  mapview(\n    google_sf,\n    col.regions = \"steelblue\",\n    cex = 4,\n    layer.name = \"Google Maps\",\n    popup = leafpop::popupTable(\n      google_sf |> st_drop_geometry() |>\n        mutate(divergence_km = round(divergence_km, 1)) |>\n        select(all_of(point_popup_cols)),\n      feature.id = FALSE, row.numbers = FALSE\n    )\n  ) +\n  mapview(\n    source_sf,\n    col.regions = \"firebrick\",\n    cex = 4,\n    layer.name = \"Source\",\n    popup = leafpop::popupTable(\n      source_sf |> st_drop_geometry() |>\n        mutate(divergence_km = round(divergence_km, 1)) |>\n        select(all_of(point_popup_cols)),\n      feature.id = FALSE, row.numbers = FALSE\n    )\n  )\n```\n\n## Divergent facilities\n\n```{r}\n#| label: divergent-table\ndivergent |>\n  mutate(divergence_km = round(divergence_km, 1)) |>\n  arrange(desc(divergence_km)) |>\n  select(\n    `ID` = canonical_id,\n    `Facility` = canonical_name,\n    `Address` = facility_address,\n    `City` = facility_city,\n    `State` = facility_state,\n `Source lon` = source_lon\n  ) |>\n  kable()\n```\n"},"elapsedMs":47}</script></tool-result></div>

<div><tool-result call-id="toolu_01BRfCZrDpLdmREx6r7L24Bd"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"status":"success","result":{"type":"text","value":"[File: 8.0KB, 204 lines, showing lines 1-204]\n     1→# Geocode facilities using Google Map...[truncated, total 9328 chars]"},"resultPreview":{"type":"code","value":"[File: 8.0KB, 204 lines, showing lines 1-204]\n# Geocode facilities using Google Maps via ggmap, then merge with\n# source-provided coordinates (Marshall Project, Vera Institute) and\n# flag divergences.\n#\n# Two pipeline functions:\n#   geocode_roster()      — sends all roster addresses to Google Maps API\n#   build_geocoded_all()  — merges Google + source coords, flags issues\n#\n# Requires: register_google(key = Sys.getenv(\"google_maps_api_key\")) called\n# before tar_make(), or set in _targets.R.\n\n# ── Haversine distance (km) ──────────────────────────────────────────────────\n# Vectorized great-circle distance between two (lat, lon) pairs.\n\n.haversine_km <- function(lat1, lon1, lat2, lon2) {\n  R <- 6371\n  to_rad <- pi / 180\n  dlat <- (lat2 - lat1) * to_rad\n  dlon <- (lon2 - lon1) * to_rad\n  a <- sin(dlat / 2)^2 +\n    cos(lat1 * to_rad) * cos(lat2 * to_rad) * sin(dlon / 2)^2\n  R * 2 * atan2(sqrt(a), sqrt(1 - a))\n}\n\n# ── Google Maps geocoding for entire roster ──────────────────────────────────\n# Geocodes every facility in facility_roster that has at least a city.\n# Returns a table with canonical_id, address_string, google_lat, google_lon.\n#\n# Wire this target with cue = tar_cue(mode = \"never\") to avoid re-geocoding.\n# To re-run: targets::tar_invalidate(facilities_google_geocoded); tar_make()\n\ngeocode_roster <- function(facility_roster) {\n  ggmap::register_google(key = Sys.getenv(\"google_maps_api_key\"), write = FALSE)\n\n  to_geocode <- facility_roster |>\n    dplyr::filter(!is.na(facility_city)) |>\n    dplyr::mutate(\n      address_string = dplyr::if_else(\n        !is.na(facility_address),\n        paste(facility_address, facility_city, facility_state, facility_zip,\n              \"USA\", sep = \", \"),\n        paste(facility_city, facility_state, \"USA\", sep = \", \")\n      )\n    ) |>\n    dplyr::select(canonical_id, address_string)\n\n  geocoded <- ggmap::mutate_geocode(to_geocode, address_string)\n\n  geocoded |>\n    dplyr::transmute(\n      canonical_id,\n      address_string,\n      google_lat = lat,\n      google_lon = lon\n    )\n}\n\n\n# ── Unified geocoded table with divergence flags ─────────────────────────────\n# Merges Google geocoding results with source-provided coordinates from\n# Marshall Project and Vera Institute. Flags address quality issues and\n# divergences between sources.\n#\n# For facilities where Google and a source agree within 1 km, lat/lon are set\n# from Google. For facilities with only one source, that source is used.\n# For divergent rows (>1 km apart), lat/lon are NA pending manual review.\n#\n# Returns one row per canonical_id with columns:\n#   canonical_id, google_lat, google_lon, source_lat, source_lon, source_name,\n#   lat, lon, geocode_source, divergence_km, address_quality\n\nbuild_geocoded_all <- function(facility_roster,\n                               facilities_google_geocoded,\n                               hold_canonical_data,\n                               vera_facilities,\n                               detloc_lookup) {\n\n  DIVERGENCE_THRESHOLD_KM <- 1\n\n  # ── Classify address quality ──\n  quality <- facility_roster |>\n    dplyr::transmute(\n      canonical_id,\n      address_quality = dplyr::case_when(\n        is.na(facility_address) & is.na(facility_city) ~ \"no_address\",\n        is.na(facility_address) ~ \"city_only\",\n        grepl(\"^P\\\\.?\\\\s*O\\\\.?\\\\s*Box\", facility_address, ignore.case = TRUE) ~\n          \"po_box\",\n        TRUE ~ \"full\"\n      )\n    )\n\n  # ── Collect source-provided coordinates ──\n  # Marshall Project: hold facilities\n  marshall <- hold_canonical_data$hold_canonical |>\n    dplyr::filter(!is.na(lat)) |>\n    dplyr::transmute(canonical_id, source_lat = lat, source_lon = lon,\n                     source_name = \"marshall_project\")\n\n  # Vera Institute: via detloc\n  vera_coords <- vera_facilities |>\n    dplyr::filter(!is.na(latitude), !is.na(longitude)) |>\n    dplyr::select(detloc, vera_lat = latitude, vera_lon = longitude) |>\n    dplyr::distinct(detloc, .keep_all = TRUE)\n\n  vera_via_detloc <- facility_roster |>\n    dplyr::filter(!is.na(detloc)) |>\n    dplyr::select(canonical_id, detloc) |>\n    dplyr::inner_join(vera_coords, by = \"detloc\") |>\n    dplyr::transmute(canonical_id, source_lat = vera_lat, source_lon = vera_lon,\n                     source_name = \"vera_institute\")\n\n  # Combine sources; prefer Marshall over Vera when both exist for same ID\n  source_coords <- dplyr::bind_rows(marshall, vera_via_detloc) |>\n    dplyr::arrange(canonical_id,\n                   match(source_name, c(\"marshall_project\", \"vera_institute\"))) |>\n    dplyr::distinct(canonical_id, .keep_all = TRUE)\n\n  # ── Merge everything ──\n  result <- facility_roster |>\n    dplyr::select(canonical_id, canonical_name,\n                  facility_address, facility_city, facility_state, facility_zip) |>\n    dplyr::left_join(quality, by = \"canonical_id\") |>\n    dplyr::left_join(\n      facilities_google_geocoded |>\n        dplyr::select(canonical_id, google_lat, google_lon),\n      by = \"canonical_id\"\n    ) |>\n    dplyr::left_join(source_coords, by = \"canonical_id\")\n\n  # ── Compute divergence ──\n  has_both <- !is.na(result$google_lat) & !is.na(result$source_lat)\n\n  result$divergence_km <- NA_real_\n  result$divergence_km[has_both] <- .haversine_km(\n    result$google_lat[has_both], result$google_lon[has_both],\n    result$source_lat[has_both], result$source_lon[has_both]\n  )\n\n  # ── Assign lat/lon ──\n  # When both sources exist and agree (<= threshold): use Google\n\n  # When only Google exists: use Google\n  # When only source exists: use source\n  # When divergent (> threshold): leave NA for manual review\n  result <- result |>\n    dplyr::mutate(\n      divergent = !is.na(divergence_km) & divergence_km > DIVERGENCE_THRESHOLD_KM,\n      lat = dplyr::case_when(\n        divergent ~ NA_real_,\n        !is.na(google_lat) ~ google_lat,\n        !is.na(source_lat) ~ source_lat,\n        TRUE ~ NA_real_\n      ),\n      lon = dplyr::case_when(\n        divergent ~ NA_real_,\n        !is.na(google_lon) ~ google_lon,\n        !is.na(source_lon) ~ source_lon,\n        TRUE ~ NA_real_\n      ),\n      geocode_source = dplyr::case_when(\n        divergent ~ \"divergent\",\n        !is.na(google_lat) & !is.na(source_lat) ~ paste0(\"google_maps+\", source_name),\n        !is.na(google_lat) ~ \"google_maps\",\n        !is.na(source_lat) ~ source_name,\n        TRUE ~ NA_character_\n      )\n    )\n\n  # ── Console reporting ──\n  n_total      <- nrow(result)\n  n_no_address <- sum(result$address_quality == \"no_address\", na.rm = TRUE)\n  n_city_only  <- sum(result$address_quality == \"city_only\", na.rm = TRUE)\n  n_po_box     <- sum(result$address_quality == \"po_box\", na.rm = TRUE)\n  n_no_coords  <- sum(is.na(result$lat) & !result$divergent, na.rm = TRUE)\n  n_divergent  <- sum(result$divergent, na.rm = TRUE)\n  n_geocoded   <- sum(!is.na(result$lat))\n\n  cli::cli_inform(c(\n    \"i\" = \"Geocoded {n_geocoded} of {n_total} facilities\",\n    \"!\" = \"{n_no_address} with no address or city (cannot geocode)\",\n    \"!\" = \"{n_city_only} with city only (no street address)\",\n    \"!\" = \"{n_po_box} with P.O. Box addresses\",\n    \"!\" = \"{n_divergent} with Google vs. source divergence > {DIVERGENCE_THRESHOLD_KM} km (lat/lon set to NA)\"\n  ))\n\n  if (n_divergent > 0) {\n    div_rows <- result |>\n      dplyr::filter(divergent) |>\n      dplyr::arrange(dplyr::desc(divergence_km))\n    cli::cli_inform(\"Divergent facilities:\")\n    for (i in seq_len(nrow(div_rows))) {\n      cli::cli_inform(c(\"*\" = \"{div_rows$canonical_name[i]} (ID {div_rows$canonical_id[i]}): {round(div_rows$divergence_km[i], 1)} km — source: {div_rows$source_name[i]}\"))\n    }\n  }\n\n  result |>\n    dplyr::select(canonical_id, canonical_name,\n                  facility_address, facility_city, facility_state, facility_zip,\n                  lat, lon, geocode_source,\n                  google_lat, google_lon, source_lat, source_lon, source_name,\n                  divergence_km, address_quality, divergent)\n}\n"},"elapsedMs":71}</script></tool-result></div>

<div><tool-call id="toolu_01BJXm3D9RhFL6KJjn7EuiS2"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"name":"write","input":{"file_path":".positai/plans/2026-03-31-0713-geocoding-source-overrides-and-archiving.md","content":"# Geocoding source overrides and archiving\n\n## Current behavior\n\n**Default coordinate sour...[truncated, total 3404 chars]"},"caption":".positai/plans/2026-03-31-0713-geocoding-source-overrides-and-archiving.md","inputPreview":{"type":"code","value":"# Geocoding source overrides and archiving\n\n## Current behavior\n\n**Default coordinate source priority** (in `build_geocoded_all()`):\n\nWhen Google and a source (Marshall or Vera) agree within 1 km, **Google is used**. When only one source exists, that source is used. When they diverge by >1 km, `lat`/`lon` are set to `NA` (pending manual review) and `geocode_source` = `\"divergent\"`. Between Marshall and Vera, **Marshall is preferred** (for hold facilities).\n\nSo the current map shows Google coordinates for the vast majority of facilities — 147 divergent facilities get no coordinates at all.\n\n**Google caching:** The `facilities_google_geocoded` target has `cue = tar_cue(mode = \"never\")`, meaning the Google API is called only once and the result is cached in the targets store indefinitely. It will not be re-requested on `tar_make()` unless manually invalidated.\n\n## Plan\n\n### 1. <div><tool-call id="toolu_01FnkPU7hH6rT8qamhLBG8Py"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"name":"read","input":{"file_path":"R/geocode.R"},"caption":"R/geocode.R"}</script></tool-call></div>

<div><tool-result call-id="toolu_01FnkPU7hH6rT8qamhLBG8Py"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"status":"success","result":{"type":"text","value":"[File: 8.0KB, 204 lines, showing lines 1-204]\n     1→# Geocode facilities using Google Map...[truncated, total 9328 chars]"},"resultPreview":{"type":"code","value":"[File: 8.0KB, 204 lines, showing lines 1-204]\n# Geocode facilities using Google Maps via ggmap, then merge with\n# source-provided coordinates (Marshall Project, Vera Institute) and\n# flag divergences.\n#\n# Two pipeline functions:\n#   geocode_roster()      — sends all roster addresses to Google Maps API\n#   build_geocoded_all()  — merges Google + source coords, flags issues\n#\n# Requires: register_google(key = Sys.getenv(\"google_maps_api_key\")) called\n# before tar_make(), or set in _targets.R.\n\n# ── Haversine distance (km) ──────────────────────────────────────────────────\n# Vectorized great-circle distance between two (lat, lon) pairs.\n\n.haversine_km <- function(lat1, lon1, lat2, lon2) {\n  R <- 6371\n  to_rad <- pi / 180\n  dlat <- (lat2 - lat1) * to_rad\n  dlon <- (lon2 - lon1) * to_rad\n  a <- sin(dlat / 2)^2 +\n    cos(lat1 * to_rad) * cos(lat2 * to_rad) * sin(dlon / 2)^2\n  R * 2 * atan2(sqrt(a), sqrt(1 - a))\n}\n\n# ── Google Maps geocoding for entire roster ──────────────────────────────────\n# Geocodes every facility in facility_roster that has at least a city.\n# Returns a table with canonical_id, address_string, google_lat, google_lon.\n#\n# Wire this target with cue = tar_cue(mode = \"never\") to avoid re-geocoding.\n# To re-run: targets::tar_invalidate(facilities_google_geocoded); tar_make()\n\ngeocode_roster <- function(facility_roster) {\n  ggmap::register_google(key = Sys.getenv(\"google_maps_api_key\"), write = FALSE)\n\n  to_geocode <- facility_roster |>\n    dplyr::filter(!is.na(facility_city)) |>\n    dplyr::mutate(\n      address_string = dplyr::if_else(\n        !is.na(facility_address),\n        paste(facility_address, facility_city, facility_state, facility_zip,\n              \"USA\", sep = \", \"),\n        paste(facility_city, facility_state, \"USA\", sep = \", \")\n      )\n    ) |>\n    dplyr::select(canonical_id, address_string)\n\n  geocoded <- ggmap::mutate_geocode(to_geocode, address_string)\n\n  geocoded |>\n    dplyr::transmute(\n      canonical_id,\n      address_string,\n      google_lat = lat,\n      google_lon = lon\n    )\n}\n\n\n# ── Unified geocoded table with divergence flags ─────────────────────────────\n# Merges Google geocoding results with source-provided coordinates from\n# Marshall Project and Vera Institute. Flags address quality issues and\n# divergences between sources.\n#\n# For facilities where Google and a source agree within 1 km, lat/lon are set\n# from Google. For facilities with only one source, that source is used.\n# For divergent rows (>1 km apart), lat/lon are NA pending manual review.\n#\n# Returns one row per canonical_id with columns:\n#   canonical_id, google_lat, google_lon, source_lat, source_lon, source_name,\n#   lat, lon, geocode_source, divergence_km, address_quality\n\nbuild_geocoded_all <- function(facility_roster,\n                               facilities_google_geocoded,\n                               hold_canonical_data,\n                               vera_facilities,\n                               detloc_lookup) {\n\n  DIVERGENCE_THRESHOLD_KM <- 1\n\n  # ── Classify address quality ──\n  quality <- facility_roster |>\n    dplyr::transmute(\n      canonical_id,\n      address_quality = dplyr::case_when(\n        is.na(facility_address) & is.na(facility_city) ~ \"no_address\",\n        is.na(facility_address) ~ \"city_only\",\n        grepl(\"^P\\\\.?\\\\s*O\\\\.?\\\\s*Box\", facility_address, ignore.case = TRUE) ~\n          \"po_box\",\n        TRUE ~ \"full\"\n      )\n    )\n\n  # ── Collect source-provided coordinates ──\n  # Marshall Project: hold facilities\n  marshall <- hold_canonical_data$hold_canonical |>\n    dplyr::filter(!is.na(lat)) |>\n    dplyr::transmute(canonical_id, source_lat = lat, source_lon = lon,\n                     source_name = \"marshall_project\")\n\n  # Vera Institute: via detloc\n  vera_coords <- vera_facilities |>\n    dplyr::filter(!is.na(latitude), !is.na(longitude)) |>\n    dplyr::select(detloc, vera_lat = latitude, vera_lon = longitude) |>\n    dplyr::distinct(detloc, .keep_all = TRUE)\n\n  vera_via_detloc <- facility_roster |>\n    dplyr::filter(!is.na(detloc)) |>\n    dplyr::select(canonical_id, detloc) |>\n    dplyr::inner_join(vera_coords, by = \"detloc\") |>\n    dplyr::transmute(canonical_id, source_lat = vera_lat, source_lon = vera_lon,\n                     source_name = \"vera_institute\")\n\n  # Combine sources; prefer Marshall over Vera when both exist for same ID\n  source_coords <- dplyr::bind_rows(marshall, vera_via_detloc) |>\n    dplyr::arrange(canonical_id,\n                   match(source_name, c(\"marshall_project\", \"vera_institute\"))) |>\n    dplyr::distinct(canonical_id, .keep_all = TRUE)\n\n  # ── Merge everything ──\n  result <- facility_roster |>\n    dplyr::select(canonical_id, canonical_name,\n                  facility_address, facility_city, facility_state, facility_zip) |>\n    dplyr::left_join(quality, by = \"canonical_id\") |>\n    dplyr::left_join(\n      facilities_google_geocoded |>\n        dplyr::select(canonical_id, google_lat, google_lon),\n      by = \"canonical_id\"\n    ) |>\n    dplyr::left_join(source_coords, by = \"canonical_id\")\n\n  # ── Compute divergence ──\n  has_both <- !is.na(result$google_lat) & !is.na(result$source_lat)\n\n  result$divergence_km <- NA_real_\n  result$divergence_km[has_both] <- .haversine_km(\n    result$google_lat[has_both], result$google_lon[has_both],\n    result$source_lat[has_both], result$source_lon[has_both]\n  )\n\n  # ── Assign lat/lon ──\n  # When both sources exist and agree (<= threshold): use Google\n\n  # When only Google exists: use Google\n  # When only source exists: use source\n  # When divergent (> threshold): leave NA for manual review\n  result <- result |>\n    dplyr::mutate(\n      divergent = !is.na(divergence_km) & divergence_km > DIVERGENCE_THRESHOLD_KM,\n      lat = dplyr::case_when(\n        divergent ~ NA_real_,\n        !is.na(google_lat) ~ google_lat,\n        !is.na(source_lat) ~ source_lat,\n        TRUE ~ NA_real_\n      ),\n      lon = dplyr::case_when(\n        divergent ~ NA_real_,\n        !is.na(google_lon) ~ google_lon,\n        !is.na(source_lon) ~ source_lon,\n        TRUE ~ NA_real_\n      ),\n      geocode_source = dplyr::case_when(\n        divergent ~ \"divergent\",\n        !is.na(google_lat) & !is.na(source_lat) ~ paste0(\"google_maps+\", source_name),\n        !is.na(google_lat) ~ \"google_maps\",\n        !is.na(source_lat) ~ source_name,\n        TRUE ~ NA_character_\n      )\n    )\n\n  # ── Console reporting ──\n  n_total      <- nrow(result)\n  n_no_address <- sum(result$address_quality == \"no_address\", na.rm = TRUE)\n  n_city_only  <- sum(result$address_quality == \"city_only\", na.rm = TRUE)\n  n_po_box     <- sum(result$address_quality == \"po_box\", na.rm = TRUE)\n  n_no_coords  <- sum(is.na(result$lat) & !result$divergent, na.rm = TRUE)\n  n_divergent  <- sum(result$divergent, na.rm = TRUE)\n  n_geocoded   <- sum(!is.na(result$lat))\n\n  cli::cli_inform(c(\n    \"i\" = \"Geocoded {n_geocoded} of {n_total} facilities\",\n    \"!\" = \"{n_no_address} with no address or city (cannot geocode)\",\n    \"!\" = \"{n_city_only} with city only (no street address)\",\n    \"!\" = \"{n_po_box} with P.O. Box addresses\",\n    \"!\" = \"{n_divergent} with Google vs. source divergence > {DIVERGENCE_THRESHOLD_KM} km (lat/lon set to NA)\"\n  ))\n\n  if (n_divergent > 0) {\n    div_rows <- result |>\n      dplyr::filter(divergent) |>\n      dplyr::arrange(dplyr::desc(divergence_km))\n    cli::cli_inform(\"Divergent facilities:\")\n    for (i in seq_len(nrow(div_rows))) {\n      cli::cli_inform(c(\"*\" = \"{div_rows$canonical_name[i]} (ID {div_rows$canonical_id[i]}): {round(div_rows$divergence_km[i], 1)} km — source: {div_rows$source_name[i]}\"))\n    }\n  }\n\n  result |>\n    dplyr::select(canonical_id, canonical_name,\n                  facility_address, facility_city, facility_state, facility_zip,\n                  lat, lon, geocode_source,\n                  google_lat, google_lon, source_lat, source_lon, source_name,\n                  divergence_km, address_quality, divergent)\n}\n"},"elapsedMs":61}</script></tool-result></div>

For facilities with only one source, that source is used.\n# For divergent rows (>1 km apart), lat/lon are NA pending manual review.\n#\n# Returns one row per canonical_id with columns:\n#   canonical_id, google_lat, google_lon, source_lat, source_lon, source_name,\n#   lat, lon, geocode_source, divergence_km, address_quality"},"elapsedMs":59}</script></tool-result></div>

All changes are in place. Here's a summary:

**Current default behavior:** When Google and a source agree (<1 km), **Google coordinates are used on maps**. When only one source exists, that source is used. When they diverge >1 km, coordinates are `NA` (147 facilities currently unresolved).

**What changed:**

**`R/geocode.R`:**
- Added `geocode_source_preference()` — an initially-empty tribble where you can list `canonical_id` + `preferred_source` (`"google_maps"`, `"vera_institute"`, or `"marshall_project"`). Rows here override the default logic, resolving divergent facilities without changing the threshold.
- Modified `build_geocoded_all()` to join preferences and apply them as the highest-priority `case_when` branch. Overridden rows get `geocode_source = "preference:google_maps"` (etc.) and `divergent = FALSE`.

**`_targets.R`:**
- `google_geocoded_file` → exports `data/google-geocoded-facilities.csv` (921 rows: `canonical_id`, `address_string`, `google_lat`, `google_lon`)
- `facilities_geocoded_all_file` → exports `data/facilities-geocoded-all.csv` (full unified table with all sources and resolved coordinates)

**Google caching:** Confirmed — `facilities_google_geocoded` uses `cue = tar_cue(mode = "never")`, so the API is never re-called on `tar_make()`. It's only re-run after an explicit `tar_invalidate()`.




## User

The search bar lacks access to the key parameters it should search: canonical ID, facility name, city, state.

## Databot

The problem is that `addSearchFeatures` can only search a single `propertyName`. To search across multiple fields, the cleanest approach is to create a composite `search_label` column that concatenates ID, name, city, and state — then search that.

<div><tool-call id="toolu_012EBN9ugQs8fmKT7P8SEi7s"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"name":"edit","input":{"file_path":"geocoding-divergence.qmd","old_string":"# Google points (blue)\ngoogle_sf <- st_as_sf(\n  divergent |> filter(!is.na(google_lat)),\n ...[truncated, total 287 chars]","new_string":"# Composite label for search (ID | name | city, state)\ndivergent <- divergent |>\n  mutate(...[truncated, total 513 chars]"},"caption":"geocoding-divergence.qmd","inputPreview":{"type":"code","value":"@@ -97,6 +97,11 @@\n   geometry = st_sfc(lines_list, crs = 4326)\n )\n \n+# Composite label for search (ID | name | city, state)\n+divergent <- divergent |>\n+  mutate(search_label = paste0(canonical_id, \" | \", canonical_name,\n+                               \" | \", facility_city, \", \", facility_state))\n+\n # Google points (blue)\n google_sf <- st_as_sf(\n   divergent |> filter(!is.na(google_lat)),\n","language":"diff"}}</script></tool-call></div>

The search bar now indexes a composite `search_label` column formatted as `"14 | Baker Correctional Institution | Sanderson, FL"`, so typing any of the canonical ID, facility name, city, or state will match. `addSearchFeatures` does substring matching against this single property.




## User

Google maps is choking on addresses like in 2145, perhaps because information is presented redundantly in both the address and the city and state. See if this pattern recurs in the data and simplify before geocoding.

Also for this address, try using "5500 Veterans Dr" instead of "5500, Veterans Dr"

<div><tool-result call-id="toolu_01Ds2KoKspnkbqJhFdFCniE1"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"status":"success","result":{"type":"content","value":[{"type":"text","text":"Output:\n# A tibble: 1 × 2\n  canonical_id facility_address                                 ...[truncated, total 262 chars]"}]},"resultPreview":{"type":"code","value":"# A tibble: 1 × 2\n  canonical_id facility_address                                       \n         <dbl> <chr>                                                  \n1         2145 5500, Veterans Dr, St Thomas 00801, U.S. Virgin Islands"},"elapsedMs":197}</script></tool-result></div>



Good picture. There are two distinct issues to fix in `geocode_roster()`:

1. **22 addresses with embedded city/state/ZIP** (all hold facilities from Marshall Project) — the redundancy means Google gets something like `"1833 29th Ave S, Birmingham, AL 35209, HOMEWOOD, AL, NA, USA"`.
2. **1 address with a spurious comma after the street number** (facility 2145: `"5500, Veterans Dr"`)

Both should be cleaned in the `address_string` construction, before sending to the API. Let me also check where these addresses originate from:

<div><tool-call id="toolu_01ATsQHqrcoP3cxUGfHdyGhR"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"name":"runCode","input":{"code":"# These are almost all hold facilities (2026+). Check their source:\nfull_addr |> \n  mutate...[truncated, total 309 chars]","intent":"Confirm source of redundant addresses"},"intent":"Confirm source of redundant addresses","inputPreview":{"type":"code","value":"# These are almost all hold facilities (2026+). Check their source:\nfull_addr |> \n  mutate(id_range = case_when(\n    canonical_id < 399 ~ \"panel (1-398)\",\n    canonical_id < 2001 ~ \"supplemental (399-2000)\",\n    canonical_id < 2187 ~ \"hold (2001-2186)\",\n    TRUE ~ \"medical (3001+)\"\n  )) |>\n  count(id_range)\n","language":"r"}}</script></tool-call></div>

<div><tool-result call-id="toolu_01ATsQHqrcoP3cxUGfHdyGhR"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"status":"success","result":{"type":"content","value":[{"type":"text","text":"Output:\n# A tibble: 2 × 2\n  id_range             n\n  <chr>            <int>\n1 hold (2001-2...[truncated, total 149 chars]"}]},"resultPreview":{"type":"code","value":"# A tibble: 2 × 2\n  id_range             n\n  <chr>            <int>\n1 hold (2001-2186)    21\n2 medical (3001+)      1"},"elapsedMs":231}</script></tool-result></div>

All from hold/medical facilities with Marshall Project addresses. Now I'll modify `geocode_roster()` to strip the redundant city/state/ZIP suffix from the address before building the geocode string, and fix the comma-after-number pattern.

<div><tool-call id="toolu_01RbN1tS8ZW2FLBebQjzCbxe"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"name":"read","input":{"file_path":"R/geocode.R","offset":31,"limit":27},"caption":"R/geocode.R:32-58"}</script></tool-call></div>

<div><tool-result call-id="toolu_01RbN1tS8ZW2FLBebQjzCbxe"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"status":"success","result":{"type":"text","value":"[File: 9.4KB, 233 lines, showing lines 32-58 (truncated)]\n    32→\n    33→geocode_roster <-...[truncated, total 986 chars]"},"resultPreview":{"type":"code","value":"[File: 9.4KB, 233 lines, showing lines 32-58 (truncated)]\n\ngeocode_roster <- function(facility_roster) {\n  ggmap::register_google(key = Sys.getenv(\"google_maps_api_key\"), write = FALSE)\n\n  to_geocode <- facility_roster |>\n    dplyr::filter(!is.na(facility_city)) |>\n    dplyr::mutate(\n      address_string = dplyr::if_else(\n        !is.na(facility_address),\n        paste(facility_address, facility_city, facility_state, facility_zip,\n              \"USA\", sep = \", \"),\n        paste(facility_city, facility_state, \"USA\", sep = \", \")\n      )\n    ) |>\n    dplyr::select(canonical_id, address_string)\n\n  geocoded <- ggmap::mutate_geocode(to_geocode, address_string)\n\n  geocoded |>\n    dplyr::transmute(\n      canonical_id,\n      address_string,\n      google_lat = lat,\n      google_lon = lon\n    )\n}\n"},"elapsedMs":78}</script></tool-result></div>



<div><tool-call id="toolu_01Rwmoxc3ad5kBEPHecXAN6W"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"name":"edit","input":{"file_path":"R/geocode.R","old_string":"geocode_roster <- function(facility_roster) {\n  ggmap::register_google(key = Sys.getenv(\"g...[truncated, total 737 chars]","new_string":"geocode_roster <- function(facility_roster) {\n  ggmap::register_google(key = Sys.getenv(\"g...[truncated, total 2489 chars]"},"caption":"R/geocode.R","inputPreview":{"type":"code","value":"@@ -36,9 +36,15 @@\n   to_geocode <- facility_roster |>\n     dplyr::filter(!is.na(facility_city)) |>\n     dplyr::mutate(\n+      # Clean address before building geocode string:\n+      # 1. Strip embedded city/state/ZIP suffix (e.g. \", Birmingham, AL 35209\")\n+      # 2. Remove spurious comma after street number (e.g. \"5500, Veterans Dr\")\n+      clean_address = .clean_address_for_geocoding(\n+        facility_address, facility_city, facility_state\n+      ),\n       address_string = dplyr::if_else(\n-        !is.na(facility_address),\n-        paste(facility_address, facility_city, facility_state, facility_zip,\n+        !is.na(clean_address),\n+        paste(clean_address, facility_city, facility_state, facility_zip,\n               \"USA\", sep = \", \"),\n         paste(facility_city, facility_state, \"USA\", sep = \", \")\n       )\n@@ -57,6 +63,45 @@\n }\n \n \n+# ── Clean addresses before geocoding ────────────────────────────────────────\n+# Strips redundant city/state/ZIP from addresses that contain full mailing\n+# addresses (common in Marshall Project hold facility data), and removes\n+# spurious commas after street numbers.\n+\n+.clean_address_for_geocoding <- function(address, city, state) {\n+  out <- address\n+\n+  # Strip \", City, ST ZIP...\" or \", City ST ZIP...\" suffix when it matches\n+  # the facility's own city/state. Use word boundary on city to avoid\n+\n+  # partial matches (e.g. \"Albany\" in \"Albany Shaker Rd\").\n+  has_suffix <- !is.na(out) & !is.na(city) & !is.na(state)\n+  if (any(has_suffix, na.rm = TRUE)) {\n+    # Build per-row regex: \", City[,]? ST ...\" or \", City[,]? State ...\"\n+    # anchored to end-ish of string (allow trailing ZIP, territory name, etc.)\n+    suffix_pattern <- paste0(\n+      \",?\\\\s*\\\\b\", stringr::str_escape(city), \"\\\\b\",\n+      \"(?:[,\\\\s]+(?:\", stringr::str_escape(state), \"|\\\\d{5}))*\",\n+      \".*$\"\n+    )\n+    cleaned <- stringr::str_replace(\n+      out[has_suffix],\n+      stringr::regex(suffix_pattern[has_suffix], ignore_case = TRUE),\n+      \"\"\n+    )\n+    # Only apply if something remains after stripping\n+    cleaned <- trimws(cleaned)\n+    keep <- nchar(cleaned) > 0\n+    out[has_suffix][keep] <- cleaned[keep]\n+  }\n+\n+  # Remove spurious comma after leading street number (\"5500, Veterans Dr\")\n+  out <- stringr::str_replace(out, \"^(\\\\d+),\\\\s+\", \"\\\\1 \")\n+\n+  out\n+}\n+\n+\n # ── Per-facility geocode source preferences ──────────────────────────────────\n # Hand-maintained list of canonical IDs where a specific geocoding source\n # should be preferred over the default logic. Populate this table as\n","language":"diff"}}</script></tool-call></div>

Now let me also add a more general fallback — strip `, <any words>, <2-letter state> <5-digit ZIP>` at the end, to catch cases where the embedded city doesn't match the roster city:

<div><tool-call id="toolu_01C5VVWJigCQAGNNCoH9zA8b"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"name":"edit","input":{"file_path":"R/geocode.R","old_string":".clean_address_for_geocoding <- function(address, city, state) {\n  out <- address\n\n  # Str...[truncated, total 1156 chars]","new_string":".clean_address_for_geocoding <- function(address, city, state) {\n  out <- address\n\n  # Str...[truncated, total 1263 chars]"},"caption":"R/geocode.R","inputPreview":{"type":"code","value":"@@ -73,12 +73,9 @@\n \n   # Strip \", City, ST ZIP...\" or \", City ST ZIP...\" suffix when it matches\n   # the facility's own city/state. Good — the first pass handles 3010 via city match (`Phoenix`). The fallback handles the ones where the embedded city doesn't match the roster city.

Here's what changed in `R/geocode.R`:

**`geocode_roster()`** now calls `.clean_address_for_geocoding()` before building the geocode string. The cleaning function applies three transformations:

1. **City-matched suffix strip** — removes `, <city>, <state> <ZIP>...` when the embedded city matches the roster city (catches 18 of 22 cases)
2. **Generic suffix strip (fallback)** — removes `, <words>, <2-letter state> <5-digit ZIP>...` even when the city doesn't match (catches the remaining 4, e.g. Birmingham Hold Room listed under Homewood)
3. **Street number comma fix** — `"5500, Veterans Dr"` → `"5500 Veterans Dr"` (1 case)

Normal addresses without embedded city/state/ZIP pass through unchanged. The Google API target uses `cue = "never"` so these changes won't take effect until you manually invalidate and re-geocode: `tar_invalidate(facilities_google_geocoded)`.




## User

These are being geocoded by Google to a USA centroid: 327, 328, 2145, 3109. Try to figure out why.

## Databot



<div><tool-call id="toolu_01MRWmu2KAUetRqujBzwfSgq"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"name":"runCode","input":{"code":"facility_roster |>\n  filter(canonical_id %in% c(327, 328, 2145, 3109)) |>\n  select(canonic...[truncated, total 176 chars]","intent":"Check addresses for the 4 centroid-geocoded facilities"},"intent":"Check addresses for the 4 centroid-geocoded facilities","inputPreview":{"type":"code","value":"facility_roster |>\n  filter(canonical_id %in% c(327, 328, 2145, 3109)) |>\n  select(canonical_id, canonical_name, facility_address, facility_city, facility_state, facility_zip)\n","language":"r"}}</script></tool-call></div>

<div><tool-result call-id="toolu_014kQVafVKf6Kh2Y6Qs9419u"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"status":"success","result":{"type":"content","value":[{"type":"text","text":"Output:\n# A tibble: 4 × 4\n  canonical_id address_string                                   ...[truncated, total 571 chars]"}]},"resultPreview":{"type":"code","value":"# A tibble: 4 × 4\n  canonical_id address_string                                    google_lat google_lon\n         <dbl> <chr>                                                  <dbl>      <dbl>\n1          327 Us Ins Detention & Deportation, San Diego, CA, 9…       38.8      -107.\n2          328 651 Federal Drive, Suite 104, Guaynabo, PR, 0096…       38.8      -107.\n3         2145 5500, Veterans Dr, St Thomas 00801, U.S. Virgin …       38.8      -107.\n4         3109 1178 Hinemlu St, Saipan, MP, NA, USA                    38.8      -107."},"elapsedMs":213}</script></tool-result></div>

All four return ~(38.8, -107) — the US geographic centroid. The common thread:

- **327** — Address is `"Us Ins Detention & Deportation"` — not a real street address, just a facility name. Google can't resolve it.
- **328** — `"651 Federal Drive, Suite 104, Guaynabo, PR, 00968-8026, USA"` — Puerto Rico address with `", USA"` appended. Google likely can't reconcile PR + USA.
- **2145** — `"5500, Veterans Dr, St Thomas 00801, U.S. Virgin Islands, ST. THOMAS, VI, NA, USA"` — redundant city/state/territory AND `", USA"` on a USVI address.
- **3109** — `"1178 Hinemlu St, Saipan, MP, NA, USA"` — Northern Mariana Islands. `MP` is not a US state, ZIP is `NA`, and `", USA"` is appended.

The pattern: **US territories (PR, VI, MP) + ", USA" suffix confuses Google**, and one has no real address at all. The fix belongs in `geocode_roster()` — territories shouldn't get `", USA"` appended, and `NA` ZIPs should be omitted.

<div><tool-call id="toolu_01JrDGMjRC9QKJKYAJbBZL4A"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"name":"runCode","input":{"code":"# Check how many facilities are in territories\nfacility_roster |>\n  filter(!is.na(facility...[truncated, total 200 chars]","intent":"Count facilities in non-state territories"},"intent":"Count facilities in non-state territories","inputPreview":{"type":"code","value":"# Check how many facilities are in territories\nfacility_roster |>\n  filter(!is.na(facility_city)) |>\n  count(facility_state) |>\n  filter(!facility_state %in% c(state.abb, \"DC\")) |>\n  arrange(desc(n))\n","language":"r"}}</script></tool-call></div>

Now let me fix `geocode_roster()`:

The four problem cases now produce sensible geocode strings:

| ID | Before | After |
|---|---|---|
| **327** | `..., San Diego, CA, 92101, USA` | Same (no territory issue — the problem here is the non-address) |
| **328** | `..., Guaynabo, PR, 00968-8026, USA` | `..., Guaynabo, 00968-8026, Puerto Rico` |
| **2145** | `5500, Veterans Dr, St Thomas 00801, ..., ST. THOMAS, VI, NA, USA` | `5500 Veterans Dr, St Thomas, U.S. Virgin Islands` |
| **3109** | `1178 Hinemlu St, Saipan, MP, NA, USA` | `1178 Hinemlu St, Saipan, Northern Mariana Islands` |

Facility 327's problem is different — its address is `"Us Ins Detention & Deportation"`, which isn't a street address at all. Google can't resolve that to a location regardless of formatting. That one will likely need a `geocode_source_preference()` entry pointing to Vera or Marshall, or a manual address fix.

To apply these changes, you'll need to invalidate and re-geocode: `tar_invalidate(facilities_google_geocoded)` then `tar_make()`. Facility 327 will probably still fail — you may want to add it to `geocode_source_preference()` once you verify the Vera coordinates are correct.

There's already a `hold_stub_address_patches()` pattern for hold facilities. For the geocoder specifically, the cleanest approach is to add a geocode address override that operates inside `geocode_roster()` — separate from the roster data itself, since this is specifically about what string to send to Google.

Added `.geocode_address_overrides()` with the manual address for facility 327, and wired it into `geocode_roster()` via `rows_update()` before the cleaning step. The override table follows the same tribble pattern as other manual patch tables in the project — add rows as needed for other facilities with bad addresses.

After `tar_invalidate(facilities_google_geocoded)` and `tar_make()`, facility 327 will geocode to 880 Front Street, San Diego.

The address now reads `"880 Front Street"` from the cleaning stage onward.

I moved the fix from the geocoding-only override (`.geocode_address_overrides()` in `geocode.R`) into `address_patches()` in `clean.R`, which runs during `clean_all_years()`. This means the corrected address will propagate through the entire pipeline: `facilities_clean` → `facilities_aggregated` → `facilities_keyed` → `facilities_panel` → `facility_roster` → geocoding.

The Guantanamo patch was also consolidated into the same `address_patches()` table (previously it was an inline tibble). The `.geocode_address_overrides()` table in `geocode.R` is now empty, reserved for cases where the roster address is fine but Google still can't resolve it.

Note: the Guantanamo patch originally only set 4 columns (no `facility_zip`). I added `facility_zip = NA_character_` to keep the tribble rectangular — this shouldn't change behavior since Guantanamo's ZIP (`34009`) comes from the spreadsheet and `rows_update` won't overwrite it with NA... actually, it will. Let me check:

<div><tool-call id="toolu_018nQbQjkCaJX7srwaKuqBaC"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"name":"runCode","input":{"code":"# Does rows_update overwrite with NA?\ntest_clean |>\n  filter(facility_name == \"JTF Camp Si...[truncated, total 135 chars]","intent":"Check if Guantanamo ZIP was overwritten with NA"},"intent":"Check if Guantanamo ZIP was overwritten with NA","inputPreview":{"type":"code","value":"# Does rows_update overwrite with NA?\ntest_clean |>\n  filter(facility_name == \"JTF Camp Six\") |>\n  select(facility_name, facility_zip)\n","language":"r"}}</script></tool-call></div>

<div><tool-result call-id="toolu_018nQbQjkCaJX7srwaKuqBaC"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"status":"success","result":{"type":"content","value":[{"type":"text","text":"Output:\n# A tibble: 1 × 2\n  facility_name facility_zip\n  <chr>         <chr>       \n1 JTF ...[truncated, total 136 chars]"}]},"resultPreview":{"type":"code","value":"# A tibble: 1 × 2\n  facility_name facility_zip\n  <chr>         <chr>       \n1 JTF Camp Six  NA"},"elapsedMs":233}</script></tool-result></div>

That's a regression — the original patch didn't touch `facility_zip`, but including it as `NA` in the tribble now overwrites it. Let me fix by using the actual ZIP:

## User

Patch JTF Camp Six with these coordinates for Geocoding: https://geohack.toolforge.org/geohack.php?pagename=Guantanamo_Migrant_Operations_Center&params=19.915_N_75.22_W_

## Databot



The coordinates from that URL are 19.915°N, 75.22°W, i.e. `lat = 19.915, lon = -75.22`. The right place for this is `geocode_source_preference()` — we know Google's geocode for Guantanamo is wrong (it returns a US centroid or mainland coordinate), so we want to override with manual coordinates.

But `geocode_source_preference()` currently only selects between existing sources (Google, Vera, Marshall). For a manually-specified coordinate, I need a slightly different mechanism. Let me check what Vera has for this facility:

<div><tool-call id="toolu_01WT4scwUpy2M4YLk9V4ns6x"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"name":"runCode","input":{"code":"facilities_geocoded_all |>\n  filter(canonical_id == 176) |>\n  select(canonical_id, canonic...[truncated, total 175 chars]","intent":"Check current geocoding state for JTF Camp Six"},"intent":"Check current geocoding state for JTF Camp Six","inputPreview":{"type":"code","value":"facilities_geocoded_all |>\n  filter(canonical_id == 176) |>\n  select(canonical_id, canonical_name, google_lat, google_lon, source_lat, source_lon, source_name, divergence_km)\n","language":"r"}}</script></tool-call></div>

<div><tool-result call-id="toolu_01WT4scwUpy2M4YLk9V4ns6x"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"status":"success","result":{"type":"content","value":[{"type":"text","text":"Output:\n# A tibble: 1 × 8\n  canonical_id canonical_name google_lat google_lon source_lat s...[truncated, total 351 chars]"}]},"resultPreview":{"type":"code","value":"# A tibble: 1 × 8\n  canonical_id canonical_name google_lat google_lon source_lat source_lon source_name \n         <dbl> <chr>               <dbl>      <dbl>      <dbl>      <dbl> <chr>       \n1          176 JTF Camp Six         19.9      -75.1       21.5      -77.8 vera_instit…\n# ℹ 1 more variable: divergence_km <dbl>"},"elapsedMs":437}</script></tool-result></div>

Interesting — Google actually returns (19.9, -75.1) which is close to the Wikipedia coordinates (19.915, -75.22). Vera has (21.5, -77.8) which is the city of Guantánamo on the Cuban mainland, ~327 km away. The correct location is the US Naval Station on the southeast tip.

Google is close but not exact. The Wikipedia/GeoHack coordinates are the authoritative ones. I'll add a manual coordinate override mechanism to `build_geocoded_all()`:

<div><tool-call id="toolu_01SJ6WScsqMNvymtic2rEWb2"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"name":"read","input":{"file_path":"R/geocode.R","offset":120,"limit":25},"caption":"R/geocode.R:121-145"}</script></tool-call></div>

Google geocoded "3100 South Hwy 281, Edinburg, TX" to (28.3, -98.1) — that's about 215 km north of Edinburg. The Vera coordinate (26.4, -98.1) is in the right area (Edinburg is at ~26.3°N in the Rio Grande Valley).

The problem is likely that "Hwy 281" is a very long highway running north-south through Texas, and Google resolved the address to a point on Hwy 281 much further north (near Alice/George West area) rather than the Edinburg segment. The longitude matches (-98.1) but the latitude is way off.

This is a Google Maps geocoding error — the address is reasonable but Google picked the wrong segment of the highway. Vera's coordinates are almost certainly correct here. You could add this to `geocode_source_preference()`:

```r
1165, "vera_institute"
```

Want me to add it?

The issue is that `addSearchFeatures` doesn't play well with mapview's internal layer structure — mapview wraps layers in ways that make the GeoJSON properties inaccessible to the search plugin. The reliable fix is to build the map directly in leaflet, which gives us full control over the layer groups.

Let me also update the library calls to remove mapview (no longer needed) and add geojsonsf:

<div><tool-call id="toolu_018JWftctw2YCEfP9yXnFS64"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"name":"edit","input":{"file_path":"geocoding-divergence.qmd","old_string":"library(targets)\nlibrary(dplyr)\nlibrary(sf)\nlibrary(mapview)\nlibrary(leaflet)\nlibrary(leaflet.extras)\nlibrary(knitr)","new_string":"library(targets)\nlibrary(dplyr)\nlibrary(sf)\nlibrary(leaflet)\nlibrary(leaflet.extras)\nlibrary(geojsonsf)\nlibrary(knitr)"},"caption":"geocoding-divergence.qmd","inputPreview":{"type":"code","value":"@@ -27,9 +27,9 @@\n library(targets)\n library(dplyr)\n library(sf)\n-library(mapview)\n library(leaflet)\n library(leaflet.extras)\n+library(geojsonsf)\n library(knitr)\n ```\n \n","language":"diff"}}</script></tool-call></div>

<div><tool-result call-id="toolu_018JWftctw2YCEfP9yXnFS64"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"status":"success","result":{"type":"text","value":"Updated geocoding-divergence.qmd"},"elapsedMs":728}</script></tool-result></div>

The approach: `addSearchFeatures` needs a GeoJSON layer (added via `addGeoJSON`) to search properties. So I add the Google points twice — once as a hidden GeoJSON layer with `search_label` as a searchable property, and once as styled `circleMarkers` for the visual display. The GeoJSON layer is hidden from the layer control and from view, but the search plugin can still index its properties. Lines and source points are plain `circleMarkers`/`polylines`.

This sidesteps the mapview compatibility issue entirely by keeping everything in native leaflet.

Google geocoded it successfully — (39.29, -76.62), which is downtown Baltimore near Hopkins Plaza. The issue isn't a Google failure; it's a 6.6 km divergence from the Vera coordinate (39.26, -76.67), which is further southwest.

The Google result looks correct — 31 Hopkins Plaza is a real office building in downtown Baltimore. The Vera coordinate is likely less precise (perhaps pointing to a general Baltimore area or a different office location).

This is a case where Google is right and Vera is off. Adding `2002, "google_maps"` to `geocode_source_preference()` would resolve it. Want me to add it?

<div><tool-call id="toolu_01GKU1LnBAHoF5TLsVwhoaSz"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"name":"runCode","input":{"code":"# Now let me systematically check: for street addresses, is Google or the source\n# more li...[truncated, total 1231 chars]","intent":"Filter to only undecided divergent facilities"},"intent":"Filter to only undecided divergent facilities","inputPreview":{"type":"code","value":"# Now let me systematically check: for street addresses, is Google or the source\n# more likely correct? <div><tool-call id="toolu_01BZcs4Tu1ZLsXbXheuUMC1h"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"name":"runCode","input":{"code":"# For the remaining 54, let me check which ones have problematic addresses\n# that make Goo...[truncated, total 1176 chars]","intent":"Identify facilities with problematic addresses where Google is unreliable"},"intent":"Identify facilities with problematic addresses where Google is unreliable","inputPreview":{"type":"code","value":"# For the remaining 54, let me check which ones have problematic addresses\n# that make Google unreliable (PO boxes, UNAVAILABLE, non-standard, territories)\n\nundecided <- div_review |>\n  filter(!canonical_id %in% already_decided) |>\n  mutate(\n    addr_issue = case_when(\n      facility_address == \"UNAVAILABLE\" ~ \"unavailable\",\n      grepl(\"^P\\\\.?[Oo]\\\\.?\\\\s*Box\", facility_address) ~ \"po_box\",\n      grepl(\"CONCOURSE|AIRPORT|MARIN IA$|^LUIS MUNOZ\", facility_address, ignore.case = TRUE) ~ \"airport\",\n      grepl(\"^Us Ins|^Bldg \", facility_address) ~ \"non_street\",\n      facility_state %in% c(\"PR\", \"VI\", \"GU\", \"MP\", \"Cuba\") ~ \"territory\",\n      TRUE ~ \"street\"\n    ),\n    # Quick check: is Google lat within reasonable bounds for the state?\n    # Most US states are between 25-49 lat. <div><tool-call id="toolu_018uUhWQzq4mBP9a7g9eYUks"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"name":"runCode","input":{"code":"# Now the main job: for the 45 street-address facilities, assess whether\n# Google or sourc...[truncated, total 1834 chars]","intent":"Compare Google vs source distance to city center for street-address facilities"},"intent":"Compare Google vs source distance to city center for street-address facilities","inputPreview":{"type":"code","value":"# Now the main job: for the 45 street-address facilities, assess whether\n# Google or source is likely correct. The typical pattern is that Google \n# resolves the street address correctly but Vera/Marshall has a less precise\n# or wrong coordinate for that facility.\n\n# Let me check a systematic comparison by looking at which source places\n# the point closer to the expected city. I'll use a simple approach:\n# geocode just the \"city, state\" and see which point is closer.\n\n# For efficiency, let's compute expected city centers from the data itself.\n# Many roster facilities in the same city have non-divergent coords — \n# use those as city reference points.\n\ncity_refs <- facilities_geocoded_all |>\n  filter(!divergent, !is.na(lat)) |>\n  left_join(\n    facility_roster |> select(canonical_id, facility_city, facility_state),\n    by = \"canonical_id\"\n  ) |>\n  group_by(facility_city, facility_state) |>\n  summarise(ref_lat = median(lat), ref_lon = median(lon), .groups = \"drop\")\n\n# Join to undecided street-address facilities\nstreet_check <- undecided |>\n  filter(addr_issue == \"street\") |>\n  left_join(city_refs, by = c(\"facility_city\", \"facility_state\")) |>\n  mutate(\n    google_to_city_km = .haversine_km(google_lat, google_lon, ref_lat, ref_lon),\n    source_to_city_km = .haversine_km(source_lat, source_lon, ref_lat, ref_lon),\n    closer = case_when(\n      is.na(ref_lat) ~ \"no_ref\",\n      google_to_city_km < source_to_city_km ~ \"google\",\n      TRUE ~ \"source\"\n    )\n  )\n\nstreet_check |>\n  select(id = canonical_id, name = canonical_name, \n         city = facility_city, st = facility_state,\n         src = source_name, km = divergence_km,\n         g2city = google_to_city_km, s2city = source_to_city_km, closer) |>\n  mutate(km = round(km, 1), g2city = round(g2city, 1), s2city = round(s2city, 1)) |>\n  print(n = 50, width = 180)\n","language":"r"}}</script></tool-call></div>

Map builds cleanly. The approach now matches the working `quarto-website` implementation:

- **Search** uses `addSearchFeatures` on `addCircleMarkers` layers (targeting "Google" and "Source" groups), with the `label` parameter providing the searchable text as `"Facility Name (City, ST)"`.
- **Three recommendation layers** (hidden by default, toggle via layer control):
  - **Rec: Google** (green) — 36 facilities where Google coordinates are preferred
  - **Rec: Vera** (purple) — 25 facilities where Vera/source coordinates are preferred
  - **Rec: Marshall** (orange) — 4 facilities where Marshall coordinates are preferred

Each recommendation layer shows only the *preferred* point (Google's coordinate for Google-recommended, source coordinate for Vera/Marshall-recommended), so you can toggle them on individually to review.

The bottom table now also includes a `Rec` column showing the recommendation for each facility.

Each recommendation layer now shows three things when toggled on:

- **Colored point** (larger) — the recommended location (blue for Google, red for Vera, orange for Marshall)
- **Grey point** (smaller, muted) — the rejected alternative
- **Connecting line** in the recommendation color

Toggle "Rec: Google" to see all 36 Google-recommended pairs at once, etc. You'll want to hide the main "Divergence lines", "Google", and "Source" layers when reviewing a recommendation layer to reduce clutter.

<div><tool-result call-id="toolu_013qwQnJv6oV9s1yP2ZQvdaf"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"status":"success","result":{"type":"content","value":[{"type":"text","text":"Output:\n# A tibble: 1 × 4\n  canonical_id canonical_name                detloc vera_type_co...[truncated, total 265 chars]"}]},"resultPreview":{"type":"code","value":"# A tibble: 1 × 4\n  canonical_id canonical_name                detloc vera_type_corrected\n         <int> <chr>                         <chr>  <chr>              \n1         1164 ERO El Paso Camp East Montana EROFCB Dedicated"},"elapsedMs":662}</script></tool-result></div>

Here's what happened: Facility 108 (Camp East Montana) has DETLOC `EPSSFTX` from the DDP matching. But DDP also has a *second* code for the same physical location — `EROFCB` ("ERO [Field Office] Camp [East Montana]"). Since `build_ddp_facility_canonical()` assigns new canonical IDs to DDP codes that aren't already mapped, `EROFCB` got a new ID (1164) instead of being linked to existing canonical 108.

The same address (6920 Digital Rd, El Paso, TX) and the "Camp East Montana" name fragment confirm these are the same facility under two DETLOCs. The fix would be to add `EROFCB` to the DETLOC lookup as an alias for canonical 108, and either drop 1164 or merge it.

Want me to add this as a manual DETLOC alias mapping so `EROFCB → 108`?

This is a clear **code transition**, not two separate facilities. The pattern shows:

- **EPSSFTX** (canonical 108) was the active code, running at 500–1,600 detainees through mid-August 2025
- **EROFCB** (1164) starts appearing in early August 2025 with small numbers, then ramps up
- By mid-September, EPSSFTX drops to 0–5 and **EROFCB takes over entirely**, reaching 3,116 by October 15

This looks like ICE retired the `EPSSFTX` code and migrated the facility's population tracking to the new `EROFCB` code. Same physical facility, same address — Camp East Montana in El Paso. The combined daily population is continuous and the handoff is smooth.

Canonical 1164 should be merged into 108, with `EROFCB` added as a second DETLOC alias. For DDP summary purposes, the two codes' populations should probably be summed (they don't double-count — the overlap period has small numbers on one side as the transition happens).




## User

Is there any prior record of using either of these codes, particularly in 2023?

<div><tool-result call-id="toolu_01UFz3LecRqwAgL5gBCu6iou"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"status":"success","result":{"type":"content","value":[{"type":"text","text":"Output:\n# A tibble: 2 × 5\n  detention_facility_code first_date last_date  first_nonzero la...[truncated, total 349 chars]"}]},"resultPreview":{"type":"code","value":"# A tibble: 2 × 5\n  detention_facility_code first_date last_date  first_nonzero last_nonzero\n  <chr>                   <date>     <date>     <date>        <date>      \n1 EPSSFTX                 2023-09-01 2025-10-15 2025-03-10    2025-09-30  \n2 EROFCB                  2023-09-01 2025-10-15 2025-08-01    2025-10-15"},"elapsedMs":331}</script></tool-result></div>

Both codes appear from the very start of DDP data (2023-09-01), but neither had any detainees until 2025:

| Code | Present since | First detainees | Last detainees | Source |
|------|---------------|-----------------|----------------|--------|
| **EPSSFTX** | 2023-09-01 | **2025-03-10** | 2025-09-30 | DDP, Vera ("El Paso Soft-Sided Facility", Hold/Staging) |
| **EROFCB** | 2023-09-01 | **2025-08-01** | 2025-10-15 | DDP, Vera ("ERO El Paso Camp East Montana", Dedicated) |

Neither code appears in DMCP (2015/2017 faclists) or Marshall Project (pre-2017). Both are in Vera's data but classified differently — EPSSFTX as "Hold/Staging" and EROFCB as "Dedicated."

So both codes were created in 2023 as placeholders and only activated in 2025. The facility itself (Camp East Montana / DOD Detention El Paso) first appears in the ICE annual stats in FY25 under canonical 108. The EPSSFTX code was active March–September 2025, then EROFCB took over in August–October 2025. Vera's different type classifications suggest ICE may have reclassified the facility from a temporary soft-sided processing site to a dedicated detention facility when they switched codes.




## User

These are distinct facilities. Read this journalistic quote: "In addition to that tent camp, the El Paso Service Processing Center, an ICE detention facility on Montana Avenue on the Eastside, held about 775 people on June 9. That facility has a capacity of about 1,000 people."

However, I think that we've mistakenly merged ICE data from EROFCB into 108=EPSSFTX. Check the pipeline.

There it is. `EPSSFTX → 108` is in `ddp_manual_strong_matches()` — it was hand-confirmed at some point, but incorrectly. The DDP name "El Paso Soft-Sided Facility" was matched to canonical 108 "Camp East Montana" (which is the DOD/CDF facility on Montana Avenue, not the tent camp).

These are two distinct facilities:
- **Canonical 108**: Camp East Montana / DOD Detention Facility at Fort Bliss — the permanent processing center on Montana Avenue (~1,000 capacity)
- **EPSSFTX**: El Paso Soft-Sided Facility — the tent camp

The incorrect manual match in `ddp_manual_strong_matches()` caused EPSSFTX's DETLOC to be assigned to canonical 108, which means the DDP daily population data for the tent camp has been attributed to the permanent facility.

The fix would be to:
1. Remove `EPSSFTX → 108` from `ddp_manual_strong_matches()`
2. Let EPSSFTX get its own canonical ID (in the 1054–1203 DDP range) as a separate facility

Want me to make that correction?





## User

The fix is actually:
1. Remove EPSSFTX → 108 from ddp_manual_strong_matches()
2. Look for a soft-sided / EPSSFTX data in the FY25 and FY26 data.
3. Assign a canonical ID < 401 like other facilities in the FY19-26 range.

The El Paso Soft-Sided Facility (EPSSFTX) **never appears in the ICE annual statistics** (FY19–FY26). It only exists in DDP daily population data. So it can't get a canonical ID in the 1–398 range from the panel — there's no row to assign it to.

Here's what the El Paso ICE data actually shows:

| Facility | Address | Type | Years |
|---|---|---|---|
| El Paso Service Processing Center | 8915 Montana Ave | SPC | FY19–FY26 |
| DOD Detention Facility / Camp East Montana | 6920 Digital Rd | DOD→CDF | FY25–FY26 |
| El Paso County Jail | 601 E. Overland | IGSA | FY26 only |

Canonical 108 is the DOD/CDF at 6920 Digital Rd (Camp East Montana), which first appears in FY25. EPSSFTX is a DDP-only facility that should get an ID in the DDP range (1054+), not the panel range.

So the fix is:
1. Remove `EPSSFTX → 108` from `ddp_manual_strong_matches()`
2. EPSSFTX will naturally get a new canonical ID in the DDP non-hold range (1054+) when the pipeline rebuilds

Want me to proceed with just step 1?





## User

Proceed with both steps. This facility is deserves the Vera address of 12501 Gateway Blvd S,El Paso,El Paso,TX,79934. The ERO / Camp Montana gets the Digital Rd address.

1193 is a DDP-range facility sourced from Vera. The name "Rapp Sec Center" comes from Vera's data. The name override and address patches for the two hold rooms need to go in different places.

For 1193's name: since it comes from `build_ddp_facility_canonical()` which uses Vera's `facility_name`, I need to add a Vera name override or a post-hoc rename. The cleanest approach is a `vera_detloc_matches()` entry or a name patch in the DDP canonical builder. But actually, the simplest is to add an override in `vera_institute.R`:

<div><tool-call id="toolu_0121YPrDZinQP553LNx4aYu4"><script type="application/json">{"version":1,"name":"grep","input":{"pattern":"vera_detloc_matches","path":"R/vera-institute.R"},"caption":"\"vera_detloc_matches\" in R/vera-institute.R","inputPreview":{"type":"code","value":"Pattern: vera_detloc_matches\nPath: R/vera-institute.R"}}</script></tool-call></div>
